\newbox\ncintdbox \newbox\ncinttbox %% noncommutative integral symbols
\setbox0=\hbox{$-$} \setbox2=\hbox{$\displaystyle\int$}
\setbox\ncintdbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
		to \wd2{\hskip-.125em \box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}
\setbox0=\hbox{$\vcenter{\hrule width 4pt}$}
\setbox2=\hbox{$\textstyle\int$} \setbox\ncinttbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
		to \wd2{\hskip-.175em \box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}

		{\copy\ncinttbox}{\copy\ncinttbox}%
		{\copy\ncinttbox}}\nolimits}  %% NC integral

	%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
	%% 2. Some internal machinery
	%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
	
	\newbox\ncintdbox \newbox\ncinttbox %% noncommutative integral symbols
	\setbox0=\hbox{$-$}
	\setbox2=\hbox{$\displaystyle\int$}
	\setbox\ncintdbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
			to \wd2{\box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}
	\setbox0=\hbox{$\vcenter{\hrule width 4pt}$}
	\setbox2=\hbox{$\textstyle\int$}
	\setbox\ncinttbox=\hbox{\rlap{\hbox
			to \wd2{\hskip-.05em\box2\relax\hfil}}\box0\kern.1em}
	
	\newcommand{\disp}{\displaystyle} %% short for  \displaystyle
	
	%\newcommand{\hideqed}{\renewcommand{\qed}{}} %% no `\qed' at end-proof

	\title{Algebraic topology of $C^*$-algebras}
	
	\author
	{\textbf{Petr R. Ivankov*}\\
		e-mail: * monster.ivankov@gmail.com \\
	}
	
	
	\begin{document}
\maketitle  %\setlength{\parindent}{0pt}
\pagestyle{plain}

\begin{abstract}
	\noindent
\paragraph{}	Any $C^*$-algebra can be regarded as a generalization of locally compact, Hausdorff topological space $\mathcal X$. From the commutative commutative Gelfand-Na\u{\i}mark theorem it follows that the spectrum of any commutative $C^*$-algebra is a locally  compact, Hausdorff space which have the exact information of the $C^*$-algebra.  Here we consider a Gelfand spaces of $C^*$-algebras which can be regarded as a generalization of the spectrum. In case of commutative $C^*$-algebras the Gelfand space coincides with the spectrum. Generally Gelfand spaces are not Hausdorff and provide more detailed information of noncommutative  $C^*$-algebras. Sometimes the Gelfand space contains the full information of noncommutative $C^*$-algebra. Usage of Gelfand spaces of $C^*$-algebra enables us to define some $C^*$-algebraic analogs of several notions of the classical algebraic topology.
\end{abstract}

\tableofcontents
\section{Gelfand category and Gelfand functor}
\paragraph{} The commutative  Gelfand-Na\u{\i}mark \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm} theorem yields the equivalence between  following categories:
\begin{itemize}
	\item  unital commutative $C^*$-algebras and $*$-homomorphisms,
		\item compact Hausdorff spaces and continuous maps.
	\end{itemize} 
	Here we would like construct a category such that objects of it are all $C^*$-algebras and a functor to the category of locally compact  Hausdorff spaces  and continuous maps.
\subsection{Basic construction}
\paragraph{} It is known that there are ultrafilters on locally compact space which are not convergent (cf. Proposition \ref{top_ultra_prop}). However from the Proposition \ref{top_ultra_prop} it follows that if an ultrafilter contains an open set with compact closure then it is convergent.
\begin{definition}\label{good_ultrafilter_defn}
An ultrafilter of open subsets sets  on locally compact Hausdorff space  is {\it good} if contains a set with compact closure.
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}\label{good_ultrafilter_rem}
From the Proposition \ref{top_ultra_prop} it follows that any locally compact Hausdorff space is a set of its good ultrafilters.
\end{remark}
Any $*$-homomorphisms $C\left( \sX\right) \to C\left( \sY\right)$ of unital yields a continuous  map $\sY\to \sX$. Any $*$-homomorphisms $C_0\left( \sX\right) \to C_b\left( \sY\right)$ can be uniquely extended up to a $*$-homomorphism $C_b\left( \sX\right) \to C_b\left( \sY\right)$ and yields a continuous map $f:\bt\sY \to \bt \sX$ where both $\bt\sX$ and $\bt \sY$ are {Stone-\v{C}ech compactifications} (cf. Definition \ref{top_stone_cech_defn}.
\begin{definition}\label{good_chom_defn}
A $*$-homomorphism $C_0\left( \sX\right) \to C_b\left( \sY\right)$ is {\it good} if it yields a  continuous map $f:\bt\sY \to \bt \sX$ such that $f\left(\sY \right)\subset \sX$. 
\end{definition}
\begin{lemma}
A homomorphism $\phi: C_0\left( \sX\right) \to C_b\left( \sY\right)$ is good  if and only if  for any $b \in C_c\left(\sY \right)$ there is  $a \in C_c\left(\sX \right)$ such that $b \in  C_0\left( \sY\right) \phi\left( a\right)$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
$\Rightarrow$ If $y\in \sY$ then there is   $b \in C_c\left(\sY \right)$ with $b\left( y\right) \neq 0$. The support $\supp b$ is compact, so the set $f\left(\supp b \right) \in \sY$ is compact.  From the Tietze theorem  is $a\in C_c \left(\sX\right)$ with $b\left( f\left(\supp b \right)\right)  = \{1\}$ and $b =  b\phi\left( a\right)$.
\\$\Leftarrow$ If $b \in C_c\left( \sY\right)$ support $\supp b$ is compact, so the set $f\left(\supp b \right) \in \sY$ is compact.  From the Tietze theorem  is $a\in C_c \left(\sX\right)$ with $a\left( f\left(\supp b\right)\right)  = \{1\}$ and $b = b\phi\left( a\right) $.
\end{proof}
\begin{definition}\label{good_hom_defn}
If both $A$ and $B$ are $C^*$-algebras  then a $*$-homomorphism $\varphi : M\left(  A\right)  \to M\left( B\right) $ is {\it good} if for any element $b \in K\left(B\right)$ of the Pedersen's ideal (cf. Definition \ref{pedersen_ideal_defn})  there is $a \in K\left(A\right)$ such that $b 
\in B\phi\left( a\right)$.
\end{definition}
\begin{definition}\label{gelfand_category_defn}
The {\it Gelfand category} $C^*$-$\mathfrak{Gelfand}$ is such that:
\begin{itemize}
	\item objects of $C^*$-$\mathfrak{Gelfand}$ are $C^*$-algebras,
	\item for any two objects $A$ and $B$ of $C^*$-$\mathfrak{Gelfand}$ the set of arrows from $A$ to $B$ is a set of good $*$-homomorphisms from $M\left(A \right)\to M\left( B\right)$, 
\end{itemize}

\end{definition}
\begin{definition}\label{lattice_a_defn}
	If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra then $A$-\textit{semi}-\textit{lattice} is the meet-semilattice (cf. Definition \ref{lattice_defn}) of closed left ideals of $A$ such that 
	\be\label{meet_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		L' \wedge L''\bydef L' \cap L'',\\
		L' \le L'' \quad \Leftrightarrow\quad L' \subset L'',\\
		0 \bydef \{0\}\subset A.
	\end{split}
	\ee
	A filter (resp, an ultrafilter) of $A$-lattice is an $A$-\textit{filter} (resp. an $A$-\textit{ultrafilter}) (cf. Definitions \ref{filter_defn} and \ref{ultra_filter_defn}).
	We denote this semilattice by $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left( A\right)$. Denote by $\mathfrak{Filters}\left( A\right)$  (resp.  $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( A\right)$) the  set of $A$-filters  (resp. $A$-ultrafilters).
\end{definition}
\begin{lemma}\label{top_lattices_iso_lem}
	For any locally compact space $\sX$ (cf. Definition \ref{top_locally_compact_defn}) there is an isomorphism of  meet-semilattices
	\be
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Lattice}_\sX : \mathfrak{Lattice}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\sX \right).
		%	L \mapsto\sX \setminus \left\{x \in \sX | \forall a \in L \quad a(x) = 0\right\}.
	\end{split}
	\ee	
	where  $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\sX \right)$ is the lattice of open subsets of $\sX$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	Any left ideal of  $C_0\left(  \sX\right)$ is a two-sided ideal. This lemma can be deduced from the proof of the Theorem \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm}.
\end{proof}
\begin{empt}\label{topology_empt}
	If $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ 
	is a set of $A$-ultrafilters (cf. Definition \ref{lattice_a_defn}) of the meet-semilattice $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left( A\right)$  then there is a topology on $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ is the minimal among topologies such that for any closed left ideal $L \subset A$ the set
	
	\be\label{topology_eqn}
	\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)_L	\bydef \left\{ \xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right) \left| \exists L' \in \xi\quad L'\subset L\right.\right\}
	\ee
	set is open.
\end{empt}
\begin{remark}
Using the direct check one can prove that the set of the  given by the equation \eqref{topology_eqn} sets is a basis of topology (cf. Definition \ref{top_base_defn}).
\end{remark}
\begin{remark}\label{compact_rem}
From the  Proposition \ref{top_ultra_prop} it follows that the space $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ is compact and Hausdorff.
\end{remark}
\begin{definition}\label{gelfand_space_defn}
	If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra then	an ultrafilter  $\xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ is an $A$-\textit{finite point} if there is a nontrivial element $a\in K\left( A\right)\setminus\{0\}$ in Pedersen's ideal (cf. Definition \ref{pedersen_ideal_defn}) such that 
	$$
	Aa \in \xi.
	$$
	The \textit{Gelfand space} $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ of $C^*$-algebra $A$ is a space  of finite points with the final topology (cf. Definition \ref{top_final_defn}) given by the natural inclusion $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \hookto \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$.
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}\label{loc_compact_rem}
	From the natural inclusion $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \hookto \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ and the Remark \ref{compact_rem} it follows that the  Gelfand  space $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ is locally compact and Hausdorff. The Gelfand  space $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ is compact if and only is the $C^*$-algebra $A$ is unital. 
\end{remark}
\begin{empt}\label{topology_base_herd_empt}
	Using the Lemma \ref{hered_ideal_lem} one can replace the closed left ideals in the Definition \ref{gelfand_space_defn} with right ones or hereditary $C^*$-subalgebras. For any filter $\xi$ we use a following notation
	\be\label{hered_ideal_eqn}
	L \in \xi \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad B \bydef L \cap L^* \in \xi\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad L^* \in \xi.
	\ee
	So the Gelfand space can be be regarded as a subset of ultrafilters of right ideals and/or a set of ultrafilters of hereditary $C^*$ subalgebras of $B \subset A$ such that there is $a \in K\left( A\right)_+$ with
	\be
	B \subset a A a
	\ee
\end{empt}

The following Lemma is a generalization of the Theorem \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm}.
\begin{lemma}\label{lem_g_lem} (Generalized commutative Gelfand theorem).
	If $\sX$ is a locally compact (cf. Definition \ref{top_locally_compact_defn}), Hausdorff space then  is a natural  homeomorphism $ \mathfrak{Gelfand}_\sX: \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left( \sX\right) \right)\cong \sX$, where  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left( \sX\right)\right)$ is the Gelfand space.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	
	From the Lemma \ref{top_lattices_iso_lem}  it turns out that for any locally compact space $\sX$ (cf. Definition \ref{top_locally_compact_defn}) there is an isomorphism of  meet-semilattices
	
	\bean
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Lattice}_\sX : \mathfrak{Lattice}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\sX \right).
		%	I \mapsto\sX \setminus \left\{x \in \sX | \forall a \in I \quad a(x) = 0\right\}.
	\end{split}
	\eean  
	It follows that there is a homeomorphism 
	$$
	\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}_\sX : \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\sX \right)
	$$ 	
	of spaces of ultrafilters. If $\xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)$ then  denote by 
	$$
	\sV_\xi\bydef 	\bigcap_{\sU \in \xi }\sU
	$$
	
	If $x \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( C_0\left(  \sX\right)\right)$ then there if $a \in K\left( C_0\left( \sX\right) \right) \cong C_c\left( \sX\right)$ such that
	$$
	aA \in \xi
	$$
	or equivalently $\sV_\xi\subset  \supp a$ and the set $\supp a$ is compact (cf. Definition \ref{top_compact_defn}).
	The set 
	$$
	\xi_a \bydef 	\left\{\left.\sU \cap \supp a \right| \sU \in \xi \right\}\in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left( {\supp a}\right) 
	$$
	is an ultrafilter on the compact set $\supp a$.
	From the Proposition \ref{top_ultra_prop} !!!!  PROP !!! it turns out that $\xi_a$ has the unique limit. This limit corresponds to $\mathfrak{Gelfand}_\sX\left( \xi\right)= \mathfrak{Gelfand}_{\supp a}\left( \xi_a\right)$. So we have the map is the set theoretic bijection. From the equation \ref{topology_eqn} one can deduce that the any open subset of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left( \sX\right)\right)$ with  corresponds to an open subset of $\sX$ and vice versa. 
\end{proof}
\paragraph*{}
If both  $A$ and $\widetilde{A}$ are $C^*$-algebras and $\varphi : A\to M\left( \widetilde{A}\right)$ is a good $*$-homomorphism (cf. Definition \ref{good_hom_defn})
%\be\label{unital_notation_eqn}
%A^\sim\bydef\begin{cases}
	%	A & \text{if }A \text{ is unital}\\
	%	A^+ & \text{if }A \text{ is not unital}\\
	%\end{cases}
	%\ee
	%where $A^+$ is given by the equation \eqref{a_plus_eqn}.
	%If $A$ is nonunital $C^*$-algebra then 	$A^{\sim}$
	%is the minimal unitization of $A$ (cf. Definition \ref{multiplier_min_defn}).
	%$If both $A$ and $\widetilde{A}$ are $C^*$-algebras then any injective  $*$-homomorphism 	
	then there is the natural homomorphism of lattices
	\be\label{lat_mor_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(  A\right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\varphi \right)}\mathfrak{Lattice} \left( \widetilde A\right),\\
		L \mapsto \text{ the $C^*$-norm closure of } \widetilde A \varphi\left(L \right).
	\end{split}
	\ee
	On the other hand the homomorphism $\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\varphi \right)$ yields a mapping of filters
	\be\label{fil_mor_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Filters}\left(  A\right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Filters}\left(\varphi \right)}\mathfrak{Filters} \left( \widetilde A\right),\\
		\left\{L_\la\right\}_{\la \in \La} \mapsto \text{ a filter generated by } \bigcup_{\la \in \La} \left\{\mathfrak{Lattice}\left(\varphi \right)\left( L_\la\right) \right\}_{\la \in \La}
	\end{split}
	\ee
	If $\xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(  A\right) $ is an ultrafilter then we define a set
	\be\label{uphi-inv_eqn}
	\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi \right)^{-1}\left(\xi \right) \bydef\left\{\left.\widetilde \xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\widetilde  A\right)\right|\forall \widetilde{L}'\in \mathfrak{Filters}\left(\varphi\right)\left( \xi\right)\subset \widetilde \xi \right\}
	\ee
	For all $\xi', \xi''\in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)$ with $\xi' \neq \xi''$ there are $L' \in \xi'$ and $L'' \in \xi''$ such that $L'\cap L'' = \{0\}$. It turns out that
	\bean
	\xi', \xi''\in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(A \right)\quad \xi' \neq \xi'' \quad \Rightarrow\\
	\Rightarrow \quad \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi \right)^{-1}\left(\xi' \right)\cap \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi \right)^{-1}\left(\xi ''\right)= \emptyset
	\eean 
	Using the above map one can construct the natural map
	\be\label{ultra_mor_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi \right)\left( \widetilde \xi\right) = \xi \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \widetilde \xi \in \mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi_M \right)^{-1}\left(\xi \right),\\
		\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\widetilde  A\right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi \right)}\mathfrak{Ultrafilters} \left( A\right).
	\end{split}
	\ee
	Since $\varphi$ is good the map \eqref{ultra_mor_eqn} naturally yields the continuous map 
	\be\label{gelfand_map_eqn}
	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)\xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\varphi \right)}\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right).
	\ee
	\begin{theorem}\label{good_thm}
		\begin{enumerate} One has
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item [(i)] 	If the  homomorphism $\varphi : M\left( A\right) \to M\left( \widetilde{A}\right)$ good 	  then the map \eqref{gelfand_map_eqn} is continuous (cf. Definition \ref{top_continuous_defn}).
				\item[(ii)] If $\varphi$ is injective then the map  \eqref{gelfand_map_eqn} is surjective.
			\end{enumerate}
	
		\end{enumerate}
		\end{theorem}
	\begin{proof}(i) 		If $L \subset A$ is a closed left ideal and 
	\bean
	\widetilde L\bydef \text{ the $C^*$-norm closure of } \widetilde A \varphi\left(L \right).
	\eean	
	then $\widetilde L$ is a closed left ideal and	
	\bean
	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\varphi \right)^{-1}\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)_L\right) \subset \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A \right)_{\widetilde L}
	\eean 
	So any  set of basis (cf. Definition \ref{top_base_defn}) of the topology of  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right)$  corresponds to a set of subbasis of the topology of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\widetilde A\right)$. From (c) of the Theorem \ref{top_continuous_thm} it turns out turns out that the map \ref{gelfand_map_eqn} is continuous. 
	
	(ii) If $\varphi$ is injective   then for any $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right)$   the given by \eqref{uphi-inv_eqn} set $\mathfrak{Ultrafilters}\left(\varphi \right)^{-1}\left(\xi \right)$ is not empty. From \eqref{ultra_mor_eqn} it follows that $\xi \in  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\varphi\right)\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A\right) \right)$.
	
\end{proof}
	 
	\begin{definition}\label{gelfand_functor_defn}
		The Theorem \ref{good_thm} yields  a contravariant {\it Gelfand functor} 
		\be\label{gelfand_functor_eqn}
		 C^*\text{-}\mathfrak{Gelfand}\xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\mathfrak{Hausdorff}
		\ee
		 Gelfand category (cf. Definition \ref{gelfand_category_defn}) to the category  $\mathfrak{Hausdorff}$ of locally compact Hausdorff topological spaces and continuous maps.  
		Any functor  $\mathfrak{Hausdorff}\to \mathscr C$ naturally yields the functor $ C^*\text{-}\mathfrak{Gelfand}
		\to \mathscr C$. This circumstance is a motivation of the term "algebraic topology of $C^*$-algebras".
	\end{definition}
	
		\begin{lemma}\label{suspension_lem}
	For any $C^*$-algebra $A$ there is the natural homeomorphism
	\be\label{suspension_g_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(SA  \right) \cong S\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right).
	\end{split}
	\ee
	\end{lemma}
	
	\begin{proof}
	There are natural injective $*$-homomorphisms 
	\bean
	\phi_A : A \hookto M\left(SA \right),\\ 
		\phi_\R : C_0\left( \R\right)  \hookto M\left(SA \right) 
	\eean
	so the Theorem \ref{good_thm}  yields surjective continuous maps
	\bean
		\varphi_A:		\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(SA \right)\onto \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A  \right),\\
						\varphi_\R:			\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(SA \right)\onto  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C_0\left(\R \right).   \right)
	\eean
	These maps naturally yield a continuous map  
		\be\label{dir_map_eqn}
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(SA \right) \to 	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A  \right)\times \R
	\end{split}
	\ee

	If $\left(x, r \right)\in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A  \right)\times \R$, both $\left\{\sU_\la\right\}_{\la\in \La}$ and $\left\{\sV_\la\right\}_{\la\in \La}$ ares bases on neighborhoods of $x$ and $r$ then $\left\{\sU_\la\times \sV_\la\right\}_{\la\in \La}$ is a  basis of neighborhoods of $\left(x, r \right)$. If $\sU_\la$ (resp. $\sV_\la$) corresponds to the closed left ideal $L^A_\la \subset A$ (resp. $L^\R_\la \subset C_0\left(\R \right)$) and
	\bean
\begin{split}
	\widetilde L^\R_\la \bydef \left\{ f \in SA \left| \supp f \in \sV_\la\right.\right\}\\
	\widetilde L^A_\la \bydef \left\{ f \in SA \left|  f\left(\R \right)  \in L^A_\la\right.\right\}\\
\end{split}
\eean
then 
	\bean
\begin{split}
	L_\la \bydef\widetilde L^\R_\la \cap \widetilde L^A_\la
\end{split}
\eean
is a closed left ideal of $A\otimes_\C C_0\left(\R \right) $. There is a filter $\left\{L_\la\right\}$. If the filter $\left\{L_\la\right\}$ is not an ultrafilter then there are $y', y'' \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(SA  \right)$ such that $y'\neq y''$ and corresponding to $y'$ and $y''$ ultrafilters  $\left\{L'_\la\right\}$ and $\left\{L''_\la\right\}$ exceed $\left\{L_\la\right\}$. There is $\la_0\in \La$ such that
	\be\label{intsec_eqn}
\begin{split}
\forall \la \in \La \quad \la \ge \la_0 \quad L'_\la \cap L''_\la = \{0\}\quad \Rightarrow \quad \left(  L'_\la\cap \widetilde L^\R_\la \cap \widetilde L^A_\la \right) \bigcap \left( L''_\la\cap \widetilde L^\R_\la \cap \widetilde L^A_\la\right)  = \{0\}
\end{split}
\ee
If $ \left( L'_\la\cap \widetilde L^A_\la\right)
\bigcap  \left( L''_\la\cap \widetilde L^A_\la\right)  = \{0\}$ for any $\la \ge \la_0$ then $\varphi_A(y')\neq  \varphi_A(y'')$ but it is impossible since $\varphi_A(y')= x$ and $\varphi_A(y'')=x$. Now the condition \eqref{intsec_eqn} holds if 
$ \left( L'_\la\cap \widetilde L^\R_\la\right)
\bigcap  \left( L''_\la\cap \widetilde L^\R_\la\right)  = \{0\}$ for any $\la \ge \la_0$. Then one has $\varphi_\R(y')\neq  \varphi_\R(y'')$ but it is impossible since $\varphi_\R(y')= r$ and $\varphi_\E(y'')=r$. So the filter $\left\{L_\la\right\}$ is an ultrafilter which yields the unique $y \in  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(SA  \right)$. In result one has a  continuous map 
\bean
\begin{split}
	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A  \right)\times \R\to 	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(SA  \right),\\
	\left(x, r \right)\mapsto y 
\end{split}
\eean
which is inverse to the map \eqref{dir_map_eqn}.

	\end{proof}
	\begin{definition}\label{image_defn}
If  $f \in C_0\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \right)$ an element $a \in M\left( A\right)$ is the \textit{image} of $f$ if for any $x \in  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ with $f\left(x \right)\neq 0$  and any $\eps > 0$ there is an ideal $L \subset A$ such that 
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item (a) $\quad x \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)_L$ (cf. equation \eqref{topology_eqn}), i.e. $L$ represents a neighborhood of $x$.
		\item(b) 	$\quad \forall b \in L \setminus \{0\}\quad   \left\| f\left( x\right) b - ab\right\| < \eps \left\| b\right\|$
			
	\end{enumerate}
We write $a = \mathfrak{Image}\left( f\right)$.
	\end{definition}
	\begin{example}\label{nt_exm} {\it Gelfand space of noncommutative torus}.
		From the Definition \ref{nt_defn} it follows that for any $j =1, ..., n$ there is an injective $*$ - homomorphism $\phi_j: C\left( U_j\right)  \hookto C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)$. Both $C^*$-algebras $C\left( U_j\right)$ and $C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)$ are unital so $\phi_j$ is good homomorphism (cf. Definition \ref{good_hom_defn}), so from the Theorem \ref{good_thm} there is a continuous map
		$$
		\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right)\xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\phi_j \right)}\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C\left( U_j\right)  \right)
		$$
		From $C\left( U_j\right) \cong C\left(S^1 \right)$ and the Lemma \ref{lem_g_lem} it follows that there is a homeomorphism  $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C\left( U_j\right)\right)   \cong S^1$, so the map $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\phi_j \right)$ is equivalent to the $\varphi_j : \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)\right) \to S^1$ one. There is the natural continuous map 
		$$
		\varphi\bydef \varphi_1 \times ... \times \varphi_n :  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)\right)  \to \underbrace{S^1\times ...\times S^1}_{n-\text{times}}\cong \T^n
		$$
		From (ii) of the Theorem \ref{good_thm} it follows that the map $\varphi_j$ is surjective for any $j = 1,..,n$. We leave to the reader the proof of that the map $\varphi$ is surjective. Let $x = \left( x_1, ..., x_n \right) \in \underbrace{S^1\times ...\times S^1}_{n-\text{times}}\cong \T^n$
		and for any $x_j \in \{x_1,...,x_n\}$ we select a basis $\left\{\sU^k_{x_j}\right\}_{k\in \N}$ of connected open neighborhoods of $x_j$. Then the net of products $\mathfrak{U}_x \bydef \left\{\sU^k_x \bydef\sU^k_{x_1}\times ...\times \sU^k_{x_n}\right\}_{k\in N}$ is a basis of neighborhoods of $x$. The net $\mathfrak{U}_x$ is an ultrafilter of $\T^n$. There is a filter $\varphi^{-1} \left( \mathfrak{U}_x\right)  \bydef \left\{\varphi^{-1}\left( \sU^k_x \right) \right\}_{k\in N}$ on $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right)$ which yields a filter of closed left ideals $\left\{L_k\subset  C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right\}$. If $\left\{L_k \right\}$ is not an ultrafilter then there is a nontrivial  closed ideal $L \subset  C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)$ such that $L \subsetneqq L_k$. It is impossible since $\bigcap L_k = \{0\}$. So $\varphi^{-1} \left( \mathfrak{U}_x\right)$ is an ultrafilter which yields the unique point which is mapped onto $x$, i.e. the map $\varphi$ is surjective. In result there is the natural bijective continuous map 
			\be\label{nt_eqn}
		\begin{split}
		\varphi : \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right) \to \T^n
		\end{split}
		\ee
		
	\end{example}
	
\subsection{$K$-theory functor}
	\paragraph{}
	Any element of $A\otimes \K$ corresponds to a matrix
	\be\label{inf_m_eqn}
	\begin{split}
	\begin{pmatrix}
		a_{1,1}& \ldots & a_{j,1} &  \dots \\
		\vdots& \ddots & \vdots& \ldots\\
		a_{j,1}& \ldots &a_{j,j} &  \ldots \\
		\vdots& \vdots & \vdots & \ddots \\
	\end{pmatrix}\in \K\left( \ell^2\left( A\right) \right)\in \K\left( L^2\left( \N \right)\right),\\
	\text{or}\\
	\begin{pmatrix}
	a_{1,1}& \ldots & a_{n,1}  \\
	\vdots& \ddots & \vdots\\
	a_{n,1}& \ldots &a_{n,n} \\
	\end{pmatrix}\in \K\left( L^2\left( \{1,...,n\} \right)\right) = \mathbb{M}_n\left(\C \right) 
	\end{split}
	\ee
	

\begin{definition}\label{elementary_defn}
	If $A$ is a  $C^*$-algebra then a given by \eqref{inf_m_eqn} element $a\in 	 \mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)$ is  $j,k$-\textit{elementary} if 
	\be\label{elementary_eqn}
	a_{p,q} = \begin{cases}
		1_A & p = j \quad q = k \\
		0 & \text{otherwise}
	\end{cases}
	\ee
\end{definition}

	\paragraph{}
	If $p \in \mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)$ is a projection then one has the natural disjoint union of open sets
	\be\label{matrppbu_eqn}
	\begin{split}
	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right)=\\= \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right)_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)p}\bigsqcup \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)\right)_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\left(1_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)} -p\right) }
\end{split}
\ee
(cf. notation \ref{topology_eqn}). From the Shilov Idempotent Theorem (cf. Appendix \ref{commutative_k_empt})  there is $p_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}} \in  C_c\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right), \Z\right)\cong H_c\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right), \Z\right)$  such that 
	\be\label{matrppbuy_eqn}
\begin{split}
 \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right)_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)p}= \left\{\left. x\in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right) \right|p_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\left( x\right)  = 1\right\},\\
  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)\right)_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\left(1_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)} -p\right) }=\\=\left\{\left. x\in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right) \right|p_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\left( x\right)  = 0\right\}
\end{split}
\ee
From \eqref{matrppbu_eqn} it turns out that 
	\bean
\begin{split}
	\mathbb{M}_n\left(C\left(  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A^+\right) \right) \right)= L \oplus L'
\end{split}
\eean
where $L$ and $L'$ are corresponding to $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)\right)_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)p}$ and\\ $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)\right)_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)\left(1_{\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)} -p\right) }$ ideals. Conversely any  projection
	\bean
\begin{split}
	\mathbb{M}_n\left(C\left(  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A^+\right) \right) \right)= L \oplus L'
\end{split}
\eean
 naturally yields an idempotent  $e \in 	\mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right)$.
Moreover $e$ is the image (cf. Definition \ref{image_defn}) of $e_{ \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right) }$, i.e.
$$
p =  \mathfrak{Image}\left( p_{ \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) }\right) .
$$
If $A$ is a stable $C^*$-algebra then for any $n \in \N$ there is $*$-isomorphisms $A^+ \cong \mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right)$ which yields a homeomorphism $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right)$. So any projector in $\mathbb{M}_n\left(A ^+\right)$  yield a projector in $C\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right) \right)$ and vice versa.
According to the  Shilov Idempotent Theorem any projector in $C\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right) \right)$ corresponds to an element of the group of cohomology $H^0_c\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right); \Z \right)$ with compact support (cf. \ref{commutative_k_empt}).  There is the action $U\left(A^+ \right)\times \mathrm{Pr}\left( A^+\right)\to \mathrm{Pr}(A)$ of the unitary group on the set of projectors. So there is the natural action $U\left(A^+ \right)\times H^0_c\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right); \Z \right)\to H^0_c\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right); \Z \right)$. Using the Definitions \ref{proj_v_defn} and \ref{k00_defn} one can deduce that 
\be\label{k_00_h_eqn}
\begin{split}
K_{00}\left(A^+ \right) \cong H^0_c\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right); \Z \right)/U\left(A^+ \right). 
\end{split}
\ee 
Taking into account the equations \eqref{stab_k1_eqn} and \eqref{royden_eqn} !!!

\begin{definition}
If $A$ is an unital $C^*$-algebra then for any $n\in \N$ the free module naturally yield a free sheaf $\mathscr A^n$ of Abelian groups on $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$. I both f $P, P'\subset A^n$ are projective submodules with $P \oplus P = A^n$ then there are sheaves of $\mathscr P$ and $\mathscr P'$ on $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ with $\mathscr P\oplus \mathscr P'= \mathscr A^n$. There {\it Chern class} of $P$ is the group
\be
 H^*_c\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right); \mathscr P \right)
\ee
	
\end{definition}


For any $n \in \N$. For any $n \im \N$ there is an injective $*$-homomorphism 
\bean
\begin{split}
\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)  \hookto A^+ \otimes \K.\\
a \mapsto a \otimes p_n
\end{split}
\eean
which yields a the continuous map
\bean
\begin{split}
	\mathbb{M}_n\left(A^+ \right)  \hookto A^+ \otimes \K.\\
	a \mapsto a \otimes p_n
\end{split}
\eean
which yields a continuous map
\be\label{mat_k_g_eqn}
\begin{split}
\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \otimes \K\right)\onto \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left(A \right)\right) .\\
\end{split}
\ee
The topology of $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \otimes \K\right)$ is minimal is initial with respect to the family of maps \eqref{mat_k_g_eqn} is continuous (cf. Definition \ref{top_init_defn}).
Any closed left ideal $L$ of $A$ yields a closed left ideal $\K_L$ generated by 
	\be\label{inf_mp_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\begin{pmatrix}
		L& \ldots & 0 &  \dots \\
		\vdots& \ddots & \vdots& \ldots\\
	0& \ldots &0 &  \ldots \\
		\vdots& \vdots & \vdots & \ddots \\
	\end{pmatrix}\in \K\left( \ell^2\left( A\right) \right).
\end{split}
\ee
The map $L \mapsto \K_L$ yields a set theoretic inclusion
\be\label{k_a_eqn}
 \varphi_{\K_A}\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)\hookto \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \otimes \K\right)
 \ee
\begin{definition}
The \textit{stable Gelfand space} $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)^s$ of $C^*$-algebra $A$ is a set $\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)^s$ supplied with the topology 
\end{definition}


So there is the natural one-to-one correspondence between idempotents of $	\mathbb{M}_n\left(C\left(   A^+ \right) \right)$ and 	$\mathbb{M}_n\left(C\left(  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right) \right) \right)$.



Both projectors $p$ and  $p_{ \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) }$ yield elements of algebraic $K$-theory (cf. Appendix \ref{algebraic_k_theory}) so we have the natural isomorphism 
\bean
\begin{split}
K_0^{\mathrm{alg}}\left(A^+ \right)\cong K_0^{\mathrm{alg}}\left(C\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A^+ \right)\right) \right) 
\end{split}
\eean
Using excision (cf. Appendix \ref{excision_empt} and the Theorem \ref{k_0_iso_thm}) of one has the isomorphism for nonunital $C^*$-algebras
\be\label{k_0_alg_iso}
\begin{split}
	K_0^{\mathrm{alg}}\left(A \right)\cong K_0^{\mathrm{alg}}\left(C_0\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)\right) \right) 
\end{split}
\ee
If $A$ is a stable $C^*$-algebra then from the Remark \ref{ho_top_rem} and the Theorem \ref{rosen_ak2_thm} the map \eqref{k_0_alg_iso} yields the natural isomorphism 
\be\label{k_0_top_iso_eqn}
\begin{split}
	K_0^{\mathrm{top}}\left(A \right)\cong K_0^{\mathrm{top}}\left(C_0\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)\right) \right) 
\end{split}
\ee

\begin{theorem}\label{alg_top_equivalence_thm}
If $\mathfrak{Stable}~	C^*\text{-}\mathfrak{Gelfand}$ is a category of stable $C^*$-algebras and good $*$-homomorphisms (cf. Definition \ref{good_hom_defn}) 	then there  the commutative diagram of functors and natural transformations 
	\be\label{alg_top_equivalence_eqn}
\begin{tikzcd}
	\mathfrak{Stable}~C^*\text{-}\mathfrak{Gelfand} \arrow[d,""]  \arrow[r, "K^{\mathrm{top}}_*"]\arrow[d,"\mathfrak{Gelfand}"]&  \mathfrak{Ab}  \arrow[d, equal]  \\
	\mathfrak{Hausdorff} \arrow[r, "K^*"]&  \mathfrak{Ab}  
\end{tikzcd}
\ee
%	\be\label{alg_top_equivalence_eqn}
%	\begin{tikzcd}
%		& & \mathfrak{Ab}\\
%		C^*\text{-}\mathfrak{Gelfand}\arrow[d, "\mathfrak{Gelfand}"] \arrow[rru, "K_*"]\ \arrow[rr, "K^{\mathrm{alg}}_*\circ (\cdot)^+"]& & \mathfrak{Ab} \arrow[u],  \arrow[dd,equal]  \\
%		\mathfrak{Hausdorff} \arrow[d, "C_0\left(\cdot \right)^+" ]&   &\\
%		\mathfrak{Alg} \arrow[rr, "K_*^{\mathrm{alg}}"]&   & \mathfrak{Ab}
%	\end{tikzcd}
%	\ee
	where $\mathfrak{Gelfand}$ is the Gelfand functor (cf. Definitions \ref{gelfand_functor_defn}), both $K^{\mathrm{top}}_*$ and $K^*$ are $K$ functors on $C^*$-algebras and topological spaces.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
	From the equation \eqref{k_0_top_iso_eqn} it follows the natural isomorphism
\bean
\begin{split}
	K_0^{\mathrm{top}}\left(A \right)\cong K_0^{\mathrm{top}}\left(C_0\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)\right) \right) 
\end{split}
\eean
On the other hand from \eqref{top_alg_eqn} one has
\bean
\begin{split}
 K_0^{\mathrm{top}}\left(C_0\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)\right) \right) \cong K^0\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \right),
\end{split}
\eean
i.e. there is the natural equivalence of functors.
\bean
\begin{split}
	K_0^{\mathrm{top}}\cong  K^0\circ \mathfrak{Gelfand}.
\end{split}
\eean
From  the Lemma \ref{suspension_lem} and the the Theorem \ref{suspension_thm} one can deduce
\bean
\begin{split}
	K_1^{\mathrm{top}}\cong  K^1\circ \mathfrak{Gelfand}.
\end{split}
\eean
 
\end{proof}
\begin{empt}
From the Appendix \ref{commutative_k_empt} any idempotent of $C_0\left( 	\mathbb{M}_n\left(C\left(  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A^+\right) \right) \right)\right)$ corresponds to  element of $H^0_c\left(	\mathbb{M}_n\left(C\left(  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A^+\right) \right) \right); \Z \right) \cong C_c\left( \sX, \Z\right)$. So any element of $$H^0_c\left(	\mathbb{M}_n\left(C\left(  \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A^+\right) \right) \right); \Z \right)$$ yields an element of $K_0^{\mathrm{alg}}\left(A^+ \right)$. From the Definition \ref{} the natural homomorphism  $K_0^{\mathrm{alg}}\left(A^+ \right)\onto K_0^{\mathrm{top}}\left(A^+ \right)$ is not in general injective.
\end{empt}

According to the Proposition \ref{k_1_prop} any $[u]\in K_1\left(A \right)$ is represented by an element $u$ of $U_n\left(A^+ \right)\cong U\left( \mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right) \right)$. Suppose that there is $u_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\in U\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right) \right)\right)$ which is the image of $u$  


is an unitary generator of $C\left(S^1 \right)$ then there is the natural $*$-homomorphism $C\left(S^1 \right)\to \mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right)$. From the Theorem \ref{good_thm} it follows that there is the natural continuous map 
	\bean
\begin{split}
f_S: \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right) \right) \xrightarrow{} C\left(S^1 \right) 
\end{split}
\eean
such that
	\bean
\begin{split}
u_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}} \bydef u_{S^1} \circ f_S \in U\left(\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right) \right) \right),\\
\left[u_{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\right]\in K^1\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right) \right)\right)\cong K_1\left(C_0\left( \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(\mathbb{M}_n\left( A^+\right)\right) \right)\right)  
\end{split}
\eean
From the Theorem  \ref{suspension_lem} it follows that \ref{gelfand_suspension_lem}

!!!



\begin{remark}
	If $A$ is a stable $C^*$-algebra then from the Theorem \ref{rosen_ak2_thm} it follows that the algebraic $K$-theory functor can be replaced with the $K$-functor of $K$-theory of $C^*$-algebras.
\end{remark}

	\begin{example}\label{nt_II_exm} {\it Gelfand space of noncommutative torus II}. According to the Example \ref{nt_exm} there is the natural given by \eqref{nt_eqn} bijective continuous map  
	\bean
	\begin{split}
		\varphi : \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right) \to \T^n
	\end{split}
	\eean
	On the other hand there  Theorem \ref{rp_nc_thm} there is the nontrivial projector $p_\th \in C\left( \T^2_\th\right) \subset C\left( \T^2_\th\right)$. Similarly to \eqref{matrppbu_eqn} there is the  natural disjoint union of open sets
	\bean
	\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right)= \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right)_{p_\th C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)}\bigsqcup \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right) \right)_{\left( 1-p_\th\right)  C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)}
	\eean 
	
\end{example}

	\subsection{Gelfand space of the noncommutative torus}
	\paragraph{} Here we find a bijective continuous map from the Gelfand space of noncommutative torus $C\left(\T^n _{\theta}\right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{nt_defn}) to the commutative torus $\T^n$.
\subsection{The map to the spectrum}
	From the Theorem \ref{good_thm} if follows that for any good inclusion $
\phi: C_0\left( 
\sX\right) \hookto M\left(A \right)$ there is the natural  open continuous map 
\be
\sX \xrightarrow{{\mathfrak{Gelfand}}\left( \phi\right)} \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left( A\right) 
\ee


\begin{definition}\label{belongs_defn}
	Let $A$ be a $C^*$ -algebra and let $\hat A$ be the spectrum of $A$ (cf. Definition \ref{spectrum_prime_primtive_defn}). An element $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$  \textit{belongs to} $x \in \hat A$ if one has
	\be\label{belongs_eqn}
	\forall L \in \xi \quad \rep_x\left(L\right) \neq \{0\} 
	\ee
	where $\rep_x : A \to B\left(\H_x \right)$ is an irreducible representation (cf. Definition  \ref{irred_defn}). 
	
\end{definition}
\begin{empt}
	Under the hypothesis of the Definition \ref{belongs_defn}  if $x', x'' \in \hat A$ with $x' \neq x''$ and $\xi\in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ belongs to both $x'$, and $x''$ then the generated by the set $\left\{ L \cap \ker_{x'}\right\}$ filter exceeds $\xi$. It is impossible since $\xi$ is an ultrafilter. Moreover
	\be\label{not_bel}
	\begin{split}
		\forall x \in \hat A \quad \xi \text{ does not belong to } x \quad \Rightarrow \quad \exists L  \in \xi \quad \rep_x\left( L\right) = \{0\}.
	\end{split}
	\ee
	
	So from (c) of the Theorem \ref{top_continuous_thm} one has the natural continuous map:
	\be\label{to_spec_eqn} 
	\begin{split}
		\mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right) \xrightarrow{\hat \phi} \hat A
	\end{split}
	\ee
\end{empt}
\begin{definition}\label{bicommutant_defn}
	Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra. If $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ and the set
	\be\label{bicommutant_id_eqn}
	\xi'' \bydef \left\{\left. a \in \rep_{\hat \phi\left( \xi\right) }\left(A \right)\right| \forall L \in \xi \quad  a^* \rep_{\hat \phi\left( \xi\right) }\left(L \right) = \{0\}
	\right\}\subset \rep_{\hat \phi\left( \xi\right) }\left(A \right)
	\ee
	is a proper left ideal of $\rep_{\hat \phi\left( \xi\right) }\left(A \right)$ then $\xi''$ is the \textit{bicommutant} of $\xi$. If for any $\xi \in \mathfrak{Gelfand}\left(A \right)$ the bicommutant exists then there is 
	is the natural surjective  map 
	\be\label{bicommutant_to_eqn}
	\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right) \xrightarrow{\phi''}  \mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''
	\ee
	where $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''$ is the set of all bicommutants. We consider the final with respect to the map $\phi''$   topology on $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''$ and say that the space $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)''$ is the \textit{bicommutant} of $\mathfrak{Gelfand} \left(A \right)$ (cf. Definition \ref{top_final_defn}).
\end{definition}
\subsection{Examples of classical and quantum projective modules}
\paragraph{Hausdorff spectrum.}
If $A$ is a homogeneous of order $n$ $C^*$-algebra (cf. Definition \ref{ctr_homo_defn}) then $A$ corresponds to a fibre bundle and any fiber  is $n^2$-dimensional $\C$-space $\mathbb{M}_n\left( 
\C\right)$. The spectrum of $\sX$ is Hausdorff and locally compact. If the space $\sX$ is  compact then both $C\left( \sX\right)$ and $A$ are unital. From the Theorem \ref{serre_swan_thm} it follows that $A$ is a finitely generated projective $C\left( \sX\right)$-module. From this fact one can deduce that any finitely generated projective $A$-module $P$ is a finitely generated projective $C\left( \sX\right) $-module, i.e. $P$ is classical (cf. Definition \ref{classic_quant_defn}).
\paragraph{Non Hausdorff spectrum.}
If  $\left(\T^2, \mathcal{F}_\th \right)$ is  the {Kronecker foliation} $dy = \th dx$ of the 2-torus $ \T^2 \bydef \R^2/\Z^2$ (cf. Example \ref{fol_tor_exm}) then from the equation \eqref{groupoid_multiplier_eqn} it turns out that there is the natural inclusion
\be\label{torus_mult_eqn}
C_0\left(\T^2 \right) \hookto M\left(C^*_r \left(\T^2, \mathcal{F}_\th \right)\right). 
\ee
One can proof that the inclusion \eqref{torus_mult_eqn} is Hausdorff blowing-up (cf. Definition \ref{blowing_defn}). If $N \bydef N_{0,1} \subset \T^2$ is given by the equation \eqref{foli_npq_eqn} then one has
\bean
C^*_r\left( \G^N_N\right) \cong C\left(\T^2_\th\right).
\eean
(cf. equation \eqref{foli_nt_eqn}). On the other hand from \eqref{foli_times_k_eqn} it turns out that
\bean
C^*_r\left(\T^2, \sF_\th \right) = C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2} \right) \cong \K\left( \E^{\T^2}_N\right) \cong \K \otimes C^*_r\left(\G^N_N  \right)\cong  \K \otimes C\left(\T^2_\th\right). 
\eean
where $\E^{\T^2}_N$ is the explained in \ref{foli_hilb_empt} $C^*$-Hilbert module. 
The maps $u_{\R^2}, v_{\R^2}: \R^2 \to \C$
\bean
u_{\R^2}\left(x,y \right)\bydef e^{2\pi i x},\\
v_{\R^2}\left(x,y \right)\bydef e^{2\pi i y}
\eean
and the natural projection $\R^2\onto \T^2 \cong \R^2/\Z^2$ yield two unitary elements
\be\label{foli_utv_eqn}
u_{\T^2}, v_{\T^2}\in C\left( \T^2\right).
\ee
If $u'_{\R^2}: \R^2 \to \C$ is such that
\bean
\forall k_1, k_2 \in \N, \quad \forall\left(x, y \right) \in \left( \left[-\pi , \pi\right), \left[-\pi , \pi\right)\right)  \quad u'_{\R^2}\left( x + 2k_1\pi, y + 2k_2\pi\right) =\\= \begin{cases}
	e^{2i\left(  x + \th y\right)  } &\left|  y \right| \le \frac{\pi}{2},\\
	e^{2 i\left(  x + \frac{\pi\th}{2}  - \th \left(y -\pi \right) \right)  } & y >\frac{\pi}{2}\\
	e^{2 i\left(  x - \frac{\pi\th}{2}  - \th \left(y +\pi \right) \right)  } & y <-\frac{\pi}{2}
\end{cases}
\eean
then $u'_{\R^2}$ is continuous and yields an unitary continuous map $u'_{\T^2}\in C\left( \T^2\right) $ which is homotopic to $u_{\T^2}$. So one has $\left[u'_{\T^2}\right]= \left[u_{\T^2}\right]\in K^1\left(
\T^2 \right)\cong K_1\left(C\left(\T^2 \right)  \right)$ (cf. Appendices \ref{top_k_sec} and \ref{ca_k_sec}). If 
\bean
\Om_{\R^2} \bydef \left\{\left. \left(x,y \right)\in \R^2 \right| y = y' + 2\pi n\quad \left|y \right| < \frac{\pi}{2}\quad n \in \Z \right\}
\eean
and the image $\Om\in \T^2$ of $\Om_{\R^2}$ is a tubular neighborhood of $N$
If both $u, v \in C\left(\G^N_N \right)$ are given by
\eqref{foli_uv_eqn} then one has
\be
\forall \xi \in \E^\Om_N \quad \xi u'_{\T^2} = u \xi
\ee
One has $E^\Om_N\cong C\left( N\right) \otimes L^2\left( -\pi, \pi\right)$ and if $\xi \in    L^2\left( -\frac{\pi}{2}, \frac{\pi}{2}\right)\setminus \{0\}$ and $p_1$ is a projection onto $\xi$ then
$$
\E^{\T^2}_N \cong \left( \E^{N}_N \otimes \xi\right)  \oplus \left( \E^{N}_N \otimes \ell^2\left(\N \right) \right) 
$$
If $\left\{\mathfrak e_2,...  \right\}\in \ell^2\left(\N \right)$ is a basis then $\left\{\mathfrak e_1, \mathfrak e_2...  \right\}\in \ell^2\left(N \right) \cong\C \mathfrak e_1 \oplus \ell^2\left(\N \right)$ is also a basis. One has
\be\label{filinf_m_eqn}
\begin{split}
	u'_{C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2} \right)}\bydef\begin{pmatrix}
		u'_{\T^2}& 0 & \ldots &0 &  \dots \\
		0&  1_{C^*_r\left( G^N_N\right) } & \ldots& 0& \ldots \\
		\vdots& \vdots &  \ddots & \vdots& \ldots\\
		0& 0 &\ldots &1_{C^*_r\left( G^N_N\right) }&  \ldots \\
		\vdots& \vdots & \vdots &\vdots & \ddots \\
	\end{pmatrix}\in U^+\left(C^*_r\left(\G^\N_\N \right)\otimes  \K\right).
\end{split}
\ee 
It is known that $K_1\left(\G^N_N  \right)= \Z\left[u\right]  + \Z\left[v\right]$ (cf. \cite{varilly:nc_intro}) it follows that $\left[ u'_{C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2} \right)}\right]\in  K_1\left( {C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2} \right)}\right) \setminus \{0\}$. If 
\bean
u_{C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2}\right)} \bydef \begin{pmatrix}
	u_{\T^2}& 0 & \ldots &0 &  \dots \\
	0&  1_{C^*_r\left( G^N_N\right) } & \ldots& 0& \ldots \\
	\vdots& \vdots &  \ddots & \vdots& \ldots\\
	0& 0 &\ldots &1_{C^*_r\left( G^N_N\right) }&  \ldots \\
	\vdots& \vdots & \vdots &\vdots & \ddots \\
\end{pmatrix}\in U^+\left(C^*_r\left(\G^\N_\N \right)\otimes  \K\right)
\eean 
then since $u'_{\T^2}$ is homotopic to $u_{\T^2}$ one has \be\label{tori_lit_eqn}\left[u\right]=\left[ u_{C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2} \right)}\right]=\left[ u'_{C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2} \right)}\right]\in  K_1\left( {C^*_r\left(\G^{\T^2}_{\T^2} \right)}\right) \setminus \{0\}\cong K_1\left( {C^*_r\left(\G^{N}_{N} \right)}\right) \setminus \{0\}.\ee
From the proof of the Proposition \ref{inv_path_prop} it follows that there are  the given by \eqref{diag_eqn} continuous maps 
$
\Phi_{\G^{N}_{N}}: [0,1] \to \mathbb{M}_2 \left(C^*_r\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)\right) \subset \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(C^*_r\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)\right)
$,  $~
\Phi_{\T^2}: [0,1] \to \mathbb{M}_2 \left(C\left(  \T^2\right)\right) \subset \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(C\left( \T^2\right) \right)
$ such that
\bean
\Phi_{\G^{N}_{N}}\left( 0\right) = 1_{ \mathbb{M}_2 \left( C^*_r\left( \G^{N}_{N}\right) \right)},\\
\Phi_{ \G^{N}_{N} }\left(1\right) = \begin{pmatrix}
	u & 0\\
	0 & u^*
\end{pmatrix};\\
\Phi_{\T^2}\left( 0\right) = 1_{ \mathbb{M}_2 \left( C\left( \T^2\right) \right)},\\
\Phi_{\T^2}\left(1\right) = \begin{pmatrix}
	u_{\T^2} & 0\\
	0 & u^*_{\T^2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\eean
There are maps
\bean
\Psi_{\G^{N}_{N}}:[0, 1] \to \mathbb{M}_2\left( C^*_r\left( \G^{N}_{N}\right)
\right),\\
t \mapsto    \Phi_{\G^{N}_{N}}\left( t\right) \begin{pmatrix}
	1_{ C^*_r\left( \G^{N}_{N}\right)} & 0\\
	0 &0
\end{pmatrix}\left( \Phi_{\G^{N}_{N}}\left( t\right)\right)^{-1};\\
\Psi_{\T^2}:[0, 1] \to \mathbb{M}_2\left( C\left( \T^2\right)
\right),\\
t \mapsto    \Phi_{\T^2}\left( t\right) \begin{pmatrix}
	1_{ C\left( \T^2\right)} & 0\\
	0 &0
\end{pmatrix}\left( \Phi_{\T^2}\left( t\right)\right)^{-1};\\
\eean
From the proof of the Theorem \ref{suspension_thm} it follows that the maps $\Psi_{G^N_N}$ and $\Psi_{\T^2}$ yield the projections  $p_{S\G^N_N} \in \mathbb{M}_2 \left(SC_r^*\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)^+ \right)\subset  \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(SC_r^*\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)^+ \right)$ and  $p_{S\T^2} \in \mathbb{M}_2 \left(SC\left(  \T^2 \right)^+\right)\subset \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(SC\left(  \T^2 \right)^+\right)$. 
Similarly to \eqref{chern_eqn} there is a diagram
\be\label{tori_chern_eqn}
\begin{tikzcd}
	\mathbb{M}_\infty \left(SC_r^*\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)^+ \right)  \ar[r,hook, "\phi"] & SC_r^*\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)^+\otimes \K
	\ar[rd,hook, "\phi_A"]  &\\
	& & 	 M\left( C_r^*\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)^+\otimes \K\right)   \\
	& \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(S C\left( \T^2\right) ^+\right)  \ar[ru,hook, "\phi_\sX"]&
\end{tikzcd}
\ee
From the homotopy between $u'_{\T^2}$ and  $u_{\T^2}$ and 
taking into account the equations \eqref{filinf_m_eqn}, \eqref{tori_lit_eqn} one can deduce that
\be\label{foli_p_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\phi_A \circ \phi \left(p_{SG^N_N}\right)\sim  \phi_\sX \left( p_{S\T^2}\right),\\
	\phi_A \circ \phi \left(p_{SG^N_N}\right)\sim_h  \phi_\sX \left( p_{S\T^2}\right) 
\end{split}
\ee
where the relations $\sim$ and $\sim_h$ is given by the Definition \ref{projection_equivalences_defn} (cf. Remark \ref{projection_equivalences_rem}). If
\be\label{chern_nt_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\sV_{S\G^N_N} \bydef p_{G^N_N}\left(SC_r^*\left(  \G^{N}_{N}\right)^+ \right)^2,  \\
	\sV_{S\T^2 }\bydef p_{S\T^2}\left( \left(SC\left(  \T^2\right)  \right)^+\right)^2 
\end{split} 
\ee
then from the equation \eqref{chern_defn_eqn}
it follows that
\be\label{chern_nt_h2_eqn}
c^H_1\left( \sV_{SG^N_N} \right) = c^H_1\left( \sV_{S\T^2 }\right)\in H^2\left(\left(S \T^2\right)^+  ;~ \Z  \right)  
\ee
where $c^H_1$ means the given by the Definitions \ref{chern_class_defn} and \ref{chern_defn} Chern classes.
One has a homeomorphism $\T^2 \cong S^1 \times S^1$ and a projector $\phi_{\T^{2};S^1}: \T^2\to S^1$ such that
\be\label{folipu_eqn}
u_{\T^2} = u_{S^1}\circ \phi_{\T^{2};S^1}
\ee
where $u_{S^1}\in U\left(C\left(S^1 \right) \right)
$ such that $K_1\left(C\left( S^1\right)  \right)= \Z\left[u_{S^1}\right]$. The map $\phi_{\T^{2};S^1}$ yields  surjective continuous maps
\be\label{chern_st_eqn}
\begin{split}
	S\T^2 \cong \left(0, 1 \right) \times \T^2 \onto SS^1 \cong \left(0, 1 \right) \times S^1,\\
	\phi_{S\T^{2};SS^1}: \left( S\T^2\right)^+    \onto\left(  SS^1 \right)^+\\
\end{split}
\ee 
From the Theorem \ref{suspension_thm} it follows that  there is a commutative diagram
\be\label{foli_sus_eqn}
\begin{tikzcd}
	K_1\left(C\left( S^1\right)  \right) \arrow[rrr, "K_1\left( C\left( \phi_{\T^{2}/S^1} \right) \right)" ]  \arrow[d, "\th_{C\left( S^1\right)}" ]&&& K_1\left(C\left( \T^2\right)  \right)\arrow[d, "\th_{C\left(\T^2 \right) }" ]\\ 
	K_0\left(S(C\left( S^1\right) \right) \arrow[rrr, "K_0\left( C\left(\phi_{S\T^{2};SS^1}\right)\right) " ] &&& K_0\left(SC\left(\T^2 \right)  \right)
\end{tikzcd}
\ee
such that
$$
\left[u_{\T^2} \right] = K_1\left( C\left( \phi_{\T^{2}/S^1} \right) \right)\left[ u_{S^1}\right].
$$
From the proof of the Proposition \ref{inv_path_prop} it follows that there is the given by \eqref{diag_eqn} continuous map 
$
\Phi_{S^1}: [0,1] \to \mathbb{M}_2 \left(C\left(  S^1\right)\right) \subset \mathbb{M}_\infty \left(C\left( S^1\right) \right)
$ such that
\bean
\Phi_{S^1}\left(0\right) = \begin{pmatrix}
	1_{C\left(S^1 \right) } & 0\\
	0 & 1_{C\left(S^1 \right) }
\end{pmatrix},\\
\Phi_{S^1}\left(1\right) = \begin{pmatrix}
	u_{S^1} & 0\\
	0 & u^*_{S^1}
\end{pmatrix}.
\eean
There  is a map 
\bean
\Psi_{S^1}:[0, 1] \to \mathbb{M}_2\left( \left(SC(S^1)\right)^+ \right)\cong \mathbb{M}_2\left( C\left( \left( SS^1\right)^+ \right)  \right),\\
t \mapsto    \Phi_{S^1}\left( t\right) \begin{pmatrix}
	1_{ C\left( S^1\right)} & 0\\
	0 &0
\end{pmatrix}\left( \Phi_{S^1}\left( t\right)\right)^{-1}.\\
\eean
From the proof of the Theorem \ref{suspension_thm} it follows that the map $\Psi_{S^1}$ the  projection  $p_{SS^1} \in \mathbb{M}_2\left( C\left( \left( SS^1\right)^+ \right)  \right)\subset \mathbb{M}_\infty\left( C\left( \left( SS^1\right)^+ \right)  \right)$. If we consider a diagram \ref{foli_sus_eqn} then from the Theorem \ref{suspension_thm} if turns out that $\th_{C\left( S^1\right)}$ is an isomorphism, so from 	$K_1\left(C\left( S^1\right)  \right)\cong K^1\left(S^1 \right)  \cong \Z\left[u_{S^1}\right]$ it turns out that 	$K_0\left(\left( S(C\left( S^1\right) \right)^+ \right)\cong K\left( \left( SS^1\right)^+ \right) \cong \Z\left[p_{S^1}\right]\oplus \Z\left[1_{SS^1}\right]$ where $1_{SS^1}$ is a trivial bundle with base $\left(SS^1 \right)^+$. Moreover one has $\left[p_{S\T^2}\right] = K_0\left( C\left(\phi_{S\T^{2};SS^1} \right)\right)\left( \left[p_{SS^1}\right]\right)$ and $p_{S\T^2}
= p_{SS^1}\circ \phi_{S\T^{2};SS^1}$. If 
\be
\sV_{SS^1}\bydef p_{S^1}\left(\left( SS^1 \right)^+  \right)^2 
\ee
then
\be\label{chern_sstt_eqn}
\sV_{S\T^2}= \phi^*_{S\T^{2};SS^1}\sV_{SS^1}
\ee
where  the projective finitely generated modules are identified with vector bundles (cf Theorem \ref{serre_swan_thm}) and $\phi^*_{S\T^{2};SS^1}\sV_{SS^1}$ means the inverse image (cf. Definition \ref{vb_inv_img_funct_defn}).
For any $x_0, x_1 \in S^2$ with $x_0\neq x_1$ there is a homeomorphism and a continuous surjective map
\be\label{chern_ss_eqn}
\begin{split}
	S^2 \setminus \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\} \cong SS^1 
	\cong \left( SS^1\right)^+\setminus \{y_0\} \cong\left(  0, 1 \right) \times S^1,\\
	\phi_{S^2; SS^1 } : S^2\onto \left( SS^1 \right)^+.
\end{split}
\ee
Taking into account the Remark \ref{k_exact_rem} and the Corollary \ref{k_exc_cor} one has an exact sequence 

\be 
\begin{tikzcd}
	K\left( \left(0, 1 \right) \times S^1\right) \cong K\left( \left(SS^1 \right)^+ \setminus \{y_0\}\right)\arrow[r, "\psi_{\left(SS^1 \right)^+ }"] \arrow[dd, "\cong"] &K\left( \left(SS^1 \right)^+   \right) \arrow[r, "\phi_{\left(SS^1 \right)^+ }"] \arrow[dd, "K\left(  \phi_{S^2; SS^1 }\right)  "] &K\left( \{y_0\} \right)\arrow[dd]\\
	~&~ &~ \\
	K\left( \left(0, 1 \right) \times S^1\right) \cong K\left(S^2  \setminus \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\}\right)\arrow[r, "\psi_{S^2 }"]  &K\left(S^2    \right) \arrow[r, "\phi_{S^2}"]  &K\left( \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\} \right)
\end{tikzcd}
\ee
From \ref{kt_kan_line_empt} it follows that $K\left(S^2 \right) \cong \Z \left[H\right] \oplus \Z \left[1_{S^2}\right]$ where $H$ is the canonical line bundle and $1_{S^2}$ is the trivial rank-one bundle.  From \eqref{foli_sus_eqn} and $K_1\left( C\left( S^1\right) \right)\cong \Z\left[u_{s^1}\right]$ it follows that $K_0\left( \left( \left(0, 1 \right) \times S^1\right) \right)\cong  \Z \th_{C\left( S^1\right)}\left(  \left[u_{S^1}\right]\right)$.
On the other hand $
\ker \phi_2 = \Z \left(\left[H\right] -\left[1_{S^2}\right] \right) 
$ so one has
$$
\forall n \in \Z \quad \psi_{S^2}\left(n \th_{C\left( S^1\right)}\left(  \left[u_{S^1}\right]\right)\right) = n\left(H- 1 \right) 
$$
If $1_{\left(SS^1 \right)^+ }$ is a trivial rank-one bundle on $\left( SS^1 \right)^{+}$ then one has $\phi^*_{S^2/\left( SS^1 \right)^+}1_{\left(SS^1 \right)^+ }\cong  1_{S^2}$. From the Theorem \ref{serre_swan_thm} it turns out that
\bean
\psi_{\left( SS^1\right)^+}\left(K\left( \left( SS^1\right)^+\setminus \{y_0\} \right)  \right) \cong \Z\left( \left[\sV_{SS^1}\right] -\left[1_{\left( SS^1 \right)^+ }\right]\right) . 
\eean 
Using diagram chasing one has
\bea
\psi_{S^2}\left(K\left(  S^2  \setminus \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\}\right)\right)  \cong \Z\left( \left[H \right] - \left[1_{S^2}\right]\right) ,\\ 
\label{chern_pp_eqn}
K\left(  \phi_{S^2; SS^1 }\right) \left( \sV_{SS^1}\right) \cong  H.
\eea
From the inclusion $S^2 \cong \C P^1 \subset \C P^\infty$ one can deduce that there is $\xi \in H^2\left( \C P^1;~\Z \right)\cong  H^2\left( \C P^\infty;~\Z \right)$ such that  $H^2\left( \C P^\infty; ~\Z \right)$ is a generated by $\xi$ unital $\Z$-algebra. From (iv) of the Theorem \ref{chern_class_thm} it follows that 
\be\label{chern_hx_eqn}
c^H_1\left(H \right) = \xi \in H^2\left( S^2; ~\Z\right)\cong H^2\left( \C P^1;~\Z \right) .
\ee
where $c^H_1\left( H\right)$ is the cohomological Chern character (cf. Definition \ref{chern_class_defn})
From the { the exact sequence of cohomology groups} (cf. equation \eqref{exact_coh_eqn}) one has
\be
\begin{split}
	H^0\left(S^2 , \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\};\Z \right) \to H^0\left(S^2 ;\Z \right)\to H^0\left(\{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\} ;\Z \right)\to \\ \to	H^1\left(S^2 , \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\};\Z \right) \to H^1\left(S^2 ;\Z \right)\to H^1\left(\{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\} ;\Z \right)\to \\ \to	H^2\left(S^2 , \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\};\Z \right) \to H^2\left(S^2 ;\Z \right)\to H^2\left(\{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\} ;\Z \right)
\end{split}
\ee
and taking into account $H^1\left(S^2 ;\Z \right)=H^2\left(\{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\} ;\Z \right)= \{0\}$ one has the isomorphism $H^2\left(S^2 , \{x_0\}\sqcup \{x_1\};\Z \right) \xrightarrow{\cong} H^2\left(S^2 ;\Z \right)$. The Exercise \ref{quot_exer} yields the natural isomorphism 
$
H^2\left(S^2 /\left(  \{x_0\}\sqcup  \{x_1\}\right) ;\Z \right) \xrightarrow{\cong} H^2\left(S^2 ;\Z \right)
$ and taking into account \eqref{chern_ss_eqn} one concludes that these isomorphisms are equivalent to the following one
$$
H^2\left(  \phi_{S^2;SS^1}\right): H^2\left(\left(SS^1 \right)^+;~\Z  \right) \xrightarrow{\cong} H^2\left(S^2;~\Z  \right).$$ 
There is the unique nontrivial $\xi_{ SS^1  }\in H^2\left(  \phi_{S^2; SS^1};~\Z\right) \in H^2\left( \left(SS^1 \right)^+ ;\Z  \right)$ such that 
\be\label{chern_xx_eqn}
\xi = H^2\left(  \phi_{S^2;SS^1 };~\Z\right)\left(\xi_{ SS^1  } \right)
\ee
From (i) of the Theorem \ref{chern_class_thm}, and the equations \eqref{chern_pp_eqn},  \eqref{chern_hx_eqn}, \eqref{chern_xx_eqn} it turns out that $c^H_1\left( \sV_{SS^1 }\right) =  \xi_{SS^1}$. There is the natural surjective continuous map
\be
\begin{split}
	\phi_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2}: \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 \onto \left( S\T^2\right)^+,\\
	\phi_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2}\left(\{y_0\} \times S^1\right) = \{z_0\},\\
	\left( S\T^2\right)^+\cong \left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1  \right) / S^1,
\end{split}
\ee
From the { the exact sequence of cohomology groups} (cf. equation \eqref{exact_coh_eqn}) and the Exercise \ref{quot_exer} one has
\bean
H^1\left(\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1\right) /S^1~;\Z   \right) \to H^1\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 ~;\Z  \right)\to  H^1\left( S^1~:\Z  \right)\to \\
\to H^2\left(\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1\right) /S^1~;\Z   \right) \to H^2\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 ~;\Z  \right)\to  H^2\left( S^1~:\Z  \right)
\eean 
One can prove that the natural homomorphism  $H^1\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 ~;\Z  \right)\onto  H^1\left( S^1~:\Z  \right)$ is surjective and $H^2\left( S^1~:\Z  \right)= \{0\}$. From these circumstances it follows that the natural homomorphism 
\be\label{}
\begin{split}
	H^2\left(\phi_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2}, \Z \right) : H^2\left( \left(S\T^2\right)^+~;~\Z   \right)\cong \\ H^2\left(\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1\right) /S^1~;\Z   \right) \xrightarrow{\cong } H^2\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 ~;\Z  \right)
\end{split}
\ee 
is an isomorphism. On the other hand there is a projection
$$
\phi_{SS^1\times S^1 ; SS^1}: \left(  SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 \onto \left(  SS^1 \right)^+
$$
onto the first factor of the direct product. From the Exercise \ref{kunn_at_exer} one  has
$$
H^2\left( \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 ~;\Z  \right) = \Z\left( \xi_{ \left(SS^1 \right)^+  } \otimes 1_{H^0\left(S^1; \Z \right) } \right) 
$$
where $\xi_{SS^1   }$ satisfies to \eqref{chern_xx_eqn}. From the above equation one can prove that the map
\be
\begin{split}
	H^2\left(\phi_{SS^1\times S^1 ; SS^1};~ \Z \right): H^2\left( SS^1; ~\Z\right) \xrightarrow{\cong }H^2\left( SS^1\times S^1; ~\Z\right),\\
	x \mapsto x \otimes 1_{H^0\left(S^1; \Z \right) }
\end{split}
\ee
is an isomorphism so, the element 
$$
\xi_{SS^1\times S^1} \bydef H^2\left(\phi_{\left( SS^1\right)^+ \times S^1 / SS^1};~ \Z \right) \left( \xi_{SS^1}\right) 
$$
is not trivial.
There is a following commutative diagram
\bean
\begin{tikzcd}
	~& \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1 \arrow[ldd, "\phi_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2}"] \arrow[rdd, "\phi_{SS^1\times S^1 ; SS^1}"] & ~\\
	~ & ~ & ~\\
	\left(S\T^2 \right)^+ \cong \left(  \left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1\right) /S^1 \arrow[rr, "\phi_{S\T^{2};SS^1}"] & ~ & \left( SS^1 \right)^+
\end{tikzcd}
\eean
From the above diagram it follows that
\bean
\phi^*_{SS^1\times S^1 ; SS^1} \sV_{SS^1} = \phi^*_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2}\circ \phi^*_{S\T^{2};SS^1} \sV_{SS^1}
\eean
and taking into account \eqref{chern_sstt_eqn} one has
\bean
\phi^*_{SS^1\times S^1 ; SS^1} \sV_{SS^1} = \phi^*_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2} \sV_{S\T^2}  
\eean 
From (i) of the Theorem \ref{chern_class_thm} it follows that 
$$
c^H_1 \left(\phi^*_{SS^1\times S^1 ; SS^1}\sV_{SS^1} \right) = \xi_{SS^1\times S^1} \in H^2\left(\left( SS^1 \right)^+ \times S^1; \Z \right) \setminus \{0\}
$$
Applying (i) of the Theorem \ref{chern_class_thm} once again one has
\bean
H^2\left(\phi_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2};~\Z \right) \left(  c^H_1\left( \sV_{S\T^2}\right) \right)  = c^H_1 \left(\phi^*_{SS^1\times S^1 ; SS^1}\sV_{SS^1} \right).
\eean 
There is the unique nontrivial $c^H_1\left( \sV_{S\T^2}\right)$ satisfying to the above equation since the map $H^2\left(\phi_{SS^1\times S^1;S\T^2};~\Z \right)$ is an isomorphism.

\begin{lemma}
	Under the above hypothesis there is the nontrivial Chern character $c^H_1\left(\sV_{S\G^N_N} \right) \in H^2\left(\left( S\T^2 \right)^+; \Z\right)\setminus\{0\} $ (cf. Definition \ref{chern_defn}) of the given by \eqref{chern_nt_eqn} element $\sV_{\G^N_N} \in V\left( \left( SC\left(\T^2_\th \right)\right)^+\right)  \cong V\left( \left(S C^*_r\left( \G^N_N\right)\right)^+ \right) $. 
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	From \eqref{chern_nt_h2_eqn} it follows that
	\be\label{chern_nt_h2p_eqn}
	c^H_1\left( \sV_{SG^N_N} \right) = c^H_1\left( \sV_{S\T^2 }\right)\in H^2\left(\left(S \T^2\right)^+  ; \Z  \right)  
	\ee
	However both the existence of  $c^H_1\left( \sV_{S\T^2 }\right)$ and the inequality $c^H_1\left( \sV_{S\T^2 }\right)\neq 0$ are already proven.
	
\end{proof}











\begin{appendices}
			\section{Category theory}
	\subsection{Categories}
	\begin{thm}\label{zorn_thm}\cite{spanier:at} (Zorn's lemma). A partially ordered set in which every  simply ordered set has an upper bound contains maximal elements.
	\end{thm}


	\begin{definition}\label{category_defn}\cite{goldblatt:topoi}
		%	Axiomatic Definition of a Category. 
		A \textit{category} $\mathscr C$ comprises: 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item[(1)] 	 a collection of things called $\mathscr C$-\textit{objects}; 
			\item[(2)] a collection of things called $\mathscr C$-\textit{arrows}  or $\mathscr C$-\textit{morphisms}; 
			\item[(3)] operations assigning to each  $\mathscr C$-arrow $f$  $\mathscr C$-object $\mathrm{dom}f$ (the 
			"domain" of $f$) and a $\mathscr C$-object $\mathrm{cod}f$ (the "codomain" of $f$). If $a =\mathrm{dom} f$  
			and $b =\mathrm{cod} f$ we display this as 
			\bean
			f: a \to b\quad \text{or}\quad  a \xrightarrow{f} b;
			\eean
			\item[(4)] an operation assigning to each pair $\left(g, f\right)$ of $\mathscr C$-arrows with $\mathrm{dom}g = \mathrm{cod} f$.
			A $\mathscr{C}$-arrow  $g\circ f$, the \textit{composite of f and g}, having $\mathrm{dom}g\circ f= \mathrm{dom}f$ and  $\mathrm{cod }g\circ f= \mathrm{cod}g$, i.e. $g\circ f:  \mathrm{dom}f \to \mathrm{cod}g$  such that the following condition obtains:
			
			\textit{	Associative Law}: Given the configuration 
			$$
			a \xrightarrow{f}	b \xrightarrow{g}	c \xrightarrow{h}d
			$$ 
			of  $\mathscr{C}$-objects and $\mathscr{C}$-arrows  then $h \circ \left(g \circ f\right)= \left(h \circ g\right)\circ f$;
			\item[(5)] an assignment to each $\mathscr{C}$-object $b$ of a $\mathscr{C}$-arrow $\mathbb{1}_b : b \to b$, called the \textit{identity arrow} on $b$, such that 
			
			\textit{Identity Law}: For any $\mathscr{C}$-arrows $f: a \to b$ and $g : b \to c$ one has
			\bean
			\mathbb{1}_b \circ f = f \quad \text{and}\quad g\circ \mathbb{1}_b= g.
			\eean
		\end{itemize}
		
	\end{definition}
	
	\begin{notation}\label{category_not}
		If $a, b$ are  $\mathscr{C}$-objects then we denote by  $\mathscr{C}\left(a, b \right)$  a family of all arrows from $a$ to $b$.
	\end{notation}
		
				
	\begin{definition}\label{initial_ob_defn}\cite{goldblatt:topoi}
		%		PAGE 43
			An object $0_{\mathscr C}$ is \textit{initial} in category $\mathscr C$ if for every $\mathscr C$-object $a$ 
		there is one and only one arrow from $0_{\mathscr C}$ to $a$ in ${\mathscr C}$. 
	\end{definition}
	\begin{definition}\label{terminal_ob_defn}\cite{goldblatt:topoi}
		%			PAGE 44
		An object $1_{\mathscr C}$ is \textit{terminal} or \textit{final} in category $\mathscr C$ if for every $\mathscr C$-object $a$ 
		there is one and only one arrow to $0_{\mathscr C}$ to $a$ in ${\mathscr C}$. 
	\end{definition}
	
	\subsection{Limits and colimits}\label{limit_sec}
	\paragraph{} Here I follow to \cite{goldblatt:topoi}. The notion of \textit{commutative diagram}, is a 
	very important aid to understanding used in category theory.
	By a 
	diagram we simply mean a display of some objects, together with some 
	arrows (here representing functions) linking the objects. The "triangle" of 
	arrows $f$, $g$, $h$ as shown is another diagram. 
	\newline
	\begin{tikzpicture}
		\matrix (m) [matrix of math nodes,row sep=3em,column sep=4em,minimum width=2em]
		{
			A & B  \\ 
			& C\\};
		\path[-stealth]
		(m-1-1) edge node [above] {$f$} (m-1-2)
		(m-1-1) edge node [left]  {$h~~$} (m-2-2)
		(m-1-2) edge node [right] {$~~g$} (m-2-2);
	\end{tikzpicture}
	\\ 	
	It will be said to \textit{commute} if $h = g\circ f$. The point is that the diagram offers 
	two paths from $A$ to $C$, either by composing to follow $f$ and then $g$, or by 
	following h directly. Commutativity means that the two paths amount to 
	the same thing. A more complex diagram, like the previous one, is said to 
	be commutative when all possible triangles that are parts of the diagram 
	are themselves commutative. This means that any two paths of arrows in 
	the diagram that start at the same object and end at the same object 
	compose to give the same overall arrow. By a \textit{diagram} $D$ in a 
	category $\mathscr C$ we simply mean a collection of $\mathscr C$-objects $d_j, d_k,...$ together 
	with some $\mathscr C$-arrows $g: d_j \to d_k$ between certain of the objects in the 
	diagram. (Possibly more than one arrow between a given pair of objects, 
	possibly none).
	\begin{definition}\label{lim_defn}
		A \textit{cone} for diagram $D$ consists of a $\mathscr C$-object $c$ together with a $\mathscr C$-arrow 
		$c\to d_j$ for each object $f_j$ in $D$, such that
		\newline
		\begin{tikzpicture}
			\matrix (m) [matrix of math nodes,row sep=3em,column sep=4em,minimum width=2em]
			{
				d_j  & & d_k \\ 
				& c  & \\};
			\path[-stealth]
			(m-1-1) edge node [above] {$g$} (m-1-3)
			(m-2-2) edge node [left]  {$f_j~~$} (m-1-1)
			(m-2-2) edge node [right] {$~~f_k$} (m-1-3);
		\end{tikzpicture}
		\\ 	
		commutes, whenever g is an arrow in the diagram $D$. We use the 
		symbolism $\left\{f_j: c\to d_j\right\}$ to denote a cone for $D$. 
		
		
		A \textit{limit} for a diagram $D$ is a $D$-cone $\left\{f_j: c\to d_j\right\}$ with the property that for 
		any other $D$-cone $\left\{f'_j: c'\to d_j\right\}$ there is exactly one arrow $f:c' \to c$ such 
		\newline
		\begin{tikzpicture}
			\matrix (m) [matrix of math nodes,row sep=3em,column sep=4em,minimum width=2em]
			{
				& d_j &  \\ 
				c'	&  & c \\};
			\path[-stealth]
			(m-2-1) edge node [above] {$g$} (m-2-3)
			(m-2-1) edge node [left]  {$f'_j~~$} (m-1-2)
			(m-2-3) edge node [right] {$~~f_j$} (m-1-2);
		\end{tikzpicture}
		\\ 	
		commutes for every object $d_j$ in $D$. 
		This limiting cone, when it exists, is said to have the \textit{universal property} 
		with respect to $D$ -cones.
		A limit for 
		diagram $D$ is unique up to isomorphism.%:- if {ft: Ń> a\} and {f-:c'Ń> d;} 			are both limits for D, then the unique commuting arrow f: c'Ń above is 			iso (its inverse is the unique commuting arrow c-Ń*c' whose existence 			follows from the fact that {/,': c' Ń> dj is a limit). 
				% It is universal amongst such cones-any other 		D-cone factors uniquely through it as in the last diagram.		
				
				
			\end{definition} 
		
			
			
\subsection{Functors}
\begin{definition}\label{functor_defn}\cite{goldblatt:topoi}
	A \textit{functor} $F$ from category $\mathscr{C}$ to category $\mathscr{D}$ is a function that assigns 
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item [(i)]
		to each $\mathscr{C}$-object $a$, a $\mathscr{D}$-object $F(a)$; 
		\item[(ii)] to each $\mathscr{C}$-arrow $f:a \to b$ a $\mathscr{D}$-arrow $F(f): F(a) \to F(b)$, 
		such that 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item[(a)]  $F\left(\mathbb 1_a\right) = \mathbb 1_{F\left(a\right)}$ for all  $\mathscr{C}$-objects $a$, i.e. the identity arrow on $a$ is assigned 
			the identity on $F\left(a\right)$,
			\item[(b)]  $F\left(g\circ f\right)=F\left(g\right)\circ F\left( f\right) $, whenever $g \circ f$ is defined. 
			This last condition states that the $F$-image of a composite of two arrows 
			is the composite of their $F$-images.
		\end{enumerate}
		
		
	\end{enumerate}
	We write $F:\mathscr{C}\to \mathscr{D}$ or  $\mathscr{C}\xrightarrow{F} \mathscr{D}$ to indicate that $F$ is a 
	functor from $
	\mathscr{C}$ to $\mathscr{D}$. Briefly then a functor is a transformation that 
	"preserves" dom's, cod's, identities and composites. 
\end{definition}
If $a$ and $b$ are  $\mathscr{C}$-objects then a functor $\mathscr{C}\xrightarrow{F} \mathscr{D}$ yields a map
\be\label{f_ab_funct_eqn}
F_{a,b}:\mathscr{C}\left(a, b \right)  \to \mathscr{D}\left( F\left(a\right), F\left(b\right)\right)  
\ee
(cf. Notation \ref{category_not}).

	
	
\subsection{Equivalence relations}

\begin{definition}\label{equivalence_relation_defn}\cite{spanier:at}
	An \textit{equivalence relation} in a set $A$ is a relation $\sim$ between elements of $A$ 
	which is \textit{reflexive} (that is, $a\sim a$ for all $a \in A$), \textit{symmetric} (that is, $a\sim a'$ 
	implies $a'\sim a$ for $a, a'\in A$), and \textit{transitive} (that is, $a\sim a'$ and $a'\sim a''$
	imply $a \sim a''$ for $a, a', a'' \in A$). The \textit{equivalence class} of $a \in A$ with 
	respect to $\sim$ is the subset $\left\{\left. a'\in A\right| a'\sim a \right\}$. The set of all equivalence classes 
	of elements of $A$ with respect to ~ is denoted by $A/\sim$ and is called a 	\textit{quotient set} of $A$. There is a \textit{projection map} $A \to A/\sim$ which sends $a\in A$ to
	its equivalence class. 
\end{definition}


\subsection{Directed sets}

\begin{definition}\label{directed_set_defn}\cite{engelking:general_topology}
	Let $\La$ be a set and $\le$ is relation on $\La$. We say that $\le$ \textit{directs} $\La$ or $\La$ is \textit{directed} by $\le$, if $\le$ has following properties:
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item [(a)] If $\la \le \mu$ and $\mu \le \nu$, then $\la \le \nu$,
		\item[(b)] For every $\la \in \La$, $\la \le \la$,
		\item[(c)] For any $\mu,\nu \in \La$ there exists a $\la \in \La$ such that $\mu \le \la$ and $\nu \le \la$.
	\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}
\begin{definition}\label{cofinal_defn}\cite{engelking:general_topology}
	A subset $\Xi \subset \La$ is said to be \textit{cofinal} in $\La$ if for every $\la \in \La$ there is $\chi \in \Xi$ such that $\la \le \chi$. 
\end{definition}

\subsection{Natural transformations}\label{natural_transformation_sec}
\paragraph{}
Here I follow to \cite{goldblatt:topoi}.
Given two categories $\mathscr C$ and $\mathscr D$ we are going to construct a category, 
denoted $\mathrm{Funct}\left(\mathscr C, \mathscr D\right)$, or $\mathscr D^{\mathscr C}$, whose objects are the functors from $\mathscr C$ to $\mathscr D$. 
We need a definition of arrow from one functor to another. Let 
$F: \mathscr C\to \mathscr D$ and $G: \mathscr C\to \mathscr D$ be two functors. For any $\mathscr C$-object $a$ we define a $\mathscr D$-arrow $\tau_a : F\left(a\right)\to  G\left(a\right)$. We require that each  $\mathscr C$-arrow $f: a \to b$  gives rise to a diagram 
\begin{tikzpicture}
	\matrix (m) [matrix of math nodes,row sep=3em,column sep=4em,minimum width=2em]
	{
		a	& F\left(a \right)  &   G\left(a \right)\\ 
		b	& F\left(b \right)  &   G\left(b \right) \\};
	\path[-stealth]
	(m-1-1) edge node [left]  {$f$} (m-2-1)
	(m-1-2) edge node [above] {$\tau_a$} (m-1-3)
	(m-2-2) edge node [above]  {$\tau_b$} (m-2-3)
	(m-1-2) edge node [left]  {$F\left( f \right)$} (m-2-2)
	(m-1-3) edge node [left]  {$G\left( f \right)$} (m-2-3);
\end{tikzpicture}
\\ 	
that commutes.
%a F(a) Ta > G(a) Ftf)  F(b) T"  G(b) that commutes. Thus  and provide a categorical way of turning the F-picture of f:a-*b into its G-picture. 
In summary then, a \textit{natural transformation} from functor $F: \mathscr C\to \mathscr D$ and $G: \mathscr C\to \mathscr D$  to functor $F: \mathscr C\to \mathscr D$ and $G: \mathscr C\to \mathscr D$  is an assignment $\tau$ that provides, for each $\mathscr C$-object $\mathscr D$-arrow $\tau_a :F(a) \to G(a)$, such that for any $\mathscr C$-arrow $f:a\to b$, the above diagram commutes in $\mathscr D$, i.e. $\tau_b \circ F(f)= G(f)\circ \tau_a$. We use the symbolism $\tau: F\to G$, or $F \xrightarrow{\tau}G$, to denote that $\tau$ is a natural transformation from $F$ to $G$. The arrows $\tau_a$ are called the \textit{components} of $a$. Now if each component $\tau_a$ of $a$ is an iso arrow in $\mathscr D$ then  case we call $\tau$ a \textit{natural isomorphism}. Each $\tau_a: F(a)\to G(a)$ then has an inverse $\tau_a^{-1}: G(a) \to F(a)$, and these $\tau^{-1}_a$'s form the components of a natural isomorphism $\tau^{-1}: G \to F$. We denote natural isomorphism by $\tau: F \cong G$. 
\begin{example}
	The identity natural transformation $\mathbb{1}_F :F\to F$ assigns to each object $a$, the identity arrow $\mathbb{1}_{F(a)}:F(a)\to F(a)$. This is clearly a natural isomorphism. 
\end{example}

\begin{definition}\label{category_equivalence_definition}\cite{goldblatt:topoi}
	A functor $F: \mathscr C\to  \mathscr D$ is called an \textit{equivalence of categories} if there 
	is a functor $G: \mathscr D\to  \mathscr C$ such that there are natural isomorphisms $\tau : 1_{\mathscr C} \cong G \circ F$, and $\sigma : 1_{\mathscr D} \cong F \circ G$, from the identity functor on ${\mathscr C}$ to $ G \circ F$, and 
	from the identity functor on ${\mathscr D}$ to $ F \circ G$.
	
	Categories $\mathscr C$ and $\mathscr D$ are \textit{equivalent},  $\mathscr C$ and $\mathscr D$ when there exists an equivalence $F: \mathscr C\to  \mathscr D$ .
\end{definition}
\subsection{Algebraic $K$-theory}\label{algebraic_k_theory}
\paragraph{} Let $R$ be a ring with unit. To define $K_0\left(R \right)$  we consider the following equivalence
relation. We say that two finitely projective $R$-modules $P$ and $Q$ are equivalent
if and only if they are isomorphic, i.e. if there is an isomorphism of
$A$-modules $P$ and $Q$ This is clearly an equivalence relation.
We note $\overline{P}$ for the equivalence class of the projective $A$-module $P$ and
$Proj(A)$ for the set of all the equivalence classes.
\begin{definition}\cite{bass,isely:akt}
%Denition 2.1 
(Milnor) The projective module group $K_0\left(R \right)$ is the group
defined by generators and relations as follows. For each elements $P$ of
$Proj(A)$ we take a generator $\left[P\right]$ and for each pair $\left[P\right]$, $\left[Q\right]$ of generators
we dene the relation
\bean
\left[P\right]+\left[Q\right]\bydef \left[P \oplus Q\right]
\eean
\end{definition}
\begin{proposition}\cite{bass,isely:akt}
%Proposition 2.2 
Every element of $K_0\left(R\right)$  can be expressed by the formal
difference $\left[P\right]-\left[Q\right]$ of two generators.

\end{proposition}
\begin{definition}\cite{bass,isely:akt}
%Denition 3.4
 Let $n \in \N$: A matrix in $GL_n\left(R \right) $ is called {\it elementary} if
it coincides with the identity matrix except for a single off-diagonal entry.
We note $E_n\left(A \right)$  the subgroup of $GL_n\left(A \right) $ generated by all the elementary
matrices.
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}\cite{bass,isely:akt}
Since $i_n : E_n\left( A\right) \subset E_{n+1}\left(R\right)$ we can embed $E_{n}\left( R\right)$ in $E_{n+1}\left( R\right)$ for all $n \in \N$.

\end{remark}

\begin{definition}\cite{bass,isely:akt}
%Denition 3.5 
We define $E(R) \bydef \bigcup_{n \in \N} E_n\left(R\right)$ 

\end{definition}
\begin{definition}\cite{bass,isely:akt}
%Denition 3.8 
(Whitehead) We define $K_1\left(A \right)$  by the quotient
\bean
K_1\left( R\right)\bydef GL\left(R \right)/E\left(R \right)
\eean
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}\label{ho_top_rem}
If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra  then $K_0\left(A \right)\cong \pi_1\left(GL^{\mathrm{top}}\left(A \right)  \right)$. Using this fact one can prove that the functor $A \mapsto K_0\left(A \otimes \K \right)$ is homotopy invariant.  
\end{remark}
\begin{empt}\label{excision_empt}
	 Here I follow to \cite{suslin:exc}. The algebraic  $K$-theory groups $K_j\left(R \right)$ of a ring with unit $R$ are defined as a homotopy groups of $BGL\left(R \right)^+$, the Quillen plus construction applied to $BGL\left(R \right)$:
	 \be\label{kr_pi_eqn}
	 \begin{split}
	 K_j\left(R \right) \cong \pi_j\left( BGL\left(R \right)^+\right) \quad j \ge 1
	 \end{split}
	 \ee
	 If $A\subset R$ is a two-sided ideal, let $F\left(R, A \right)$ denote the homotopy of the map $ BGL\left(R \right)^+\to \overline{BGL}\left(R/A \right)^+$, where $ \overline {GL}\left(R \right)\bydef \im \left(GL\left(R \right)\to GL\left(R /A\right) \right)$. The relative $K$-groups $K_j\left(R, A \right), \quad j \ge 1$, are defined as homotopy groups of $F\left(R, A \right)$ so that one gets, with respect to a pair $\left(R. A \right)$, a functorial long exact sequence  
	 \be\label{kr_spi_eqn}
	 \begin{split}
	 	K_j\left(R \right)\to 	K_j\left(R, A \right)\to 	K_j\left(R/A \right)\to 	K_{j-1}\left(R, A \right) \to ...\\
	 	\to K_1\left(R \right)\to 	K_1\left(R, A \right)\to 	K_1\left(R/A \right).
	 \end{split}
	 \ee
	 Algebraic $K$-theory is extended to the category of rings by setting
	 \be\label{kr_npi_eqn}
	 \begin{split}
	 K_j\left( A\right) = K_j\left(\widetilde A, A \right) \quad j \ge 1,
	 \end{split}
	 \ee
where $	 \widetilde A= \Z \rtimes A$ denotes the ring obtained from $A$ by adjoining the unit.

A ring $A$ is said to satisfy {\it excision}  in algebraic $K$-theory if for every ring with unit $R$, which contains $A$ as a two-sided ideal, the canonical map $K_*\left( A\right) \to K_*\left(R, A\right)$ is an isomorphism.
\end{empt}



\section{Topology}
			\subsection{General topology}
	
	\begin{definition}\label{top_base_defn}\cite{munkres:topology}
		If $\sX$ is a set, a \textit{basis} for a topology on $\sX$ is a collection $\mathscr B$ of subsets of $\sX$
		(called \textit{basis elements}) such that:
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item [(a)]  for each $x\in \sX$, there is at least one basis element $B$ containing $x$,
			\item [(b)]  if $x$ belongs to the intersection of two basis elements $B_1$ and $B_2$, then there is a
			basis element $B_3$ containing $x$ such that $B_3 \subset B_1\cap B_2$.
		\end{enumerate}
		
		If  $\mathscr B$ satisfies these two conditions, then we define the \textit{topology}  $\mathscr T$ \textit{generated by}  $\mathscr B$ as
		follows: A subset $\sU$ of $\sX$ is said to be \textit{open} in $\sX$ (that is, to be an element of $\mathscr T$) if for
		each $x \in \sU$, there is a basis element $B \in \mathscr B$ such that $x \in B$ and $B \subset \sU$.
	\end{definition}
	\begin{remark}\label{top_base_rem}It is proven that given by the Definition \ref{top_base_defn} collection $\mathscr T$ is a topology  (cf. \cite{munkres:topology}).
	\end{remark}
	\begin{theorem}\label{top_continuous_thm}\cite{kelley:gt}
		If $\sX$ and $\sY$ are topological space and $f$ is a function 
		on $\sX$ to $\sY$, then the following statements are equivalent. 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item[ (a)] The function $f$ is continuous. 
			\item[ (b)] The inverse of each closed set is closed. 
			\item[ (c)] The inverse of each member of a subbasis for the topology for 
			$\sY$ is open. 
			\item[ (d)] For each $x$ in $\sX$ the inverse of every neighborhood of $f(x)$ is 
			a neighborhood of $x$. 
			\item[ (e)] For each $x$ in $\sX$ and each neighborhood $\sU$ of $f(x)$  there is a 
			neighborhood $\sV$ of $x$ such that $f(\sV)\subset \sU$. 
			\item[ (f)]For each net $S$  in $\sX$ which converges to a 
			point $s$, the composition $f \circ S$ converges to 
			f(s)). 
			\item[ (g)] For each subset $A$ of X the image of the closure is a subset of
